<div id="theReview">
<h2>Sucker Punch</h2>
<p class="ratd"> Rated <em>M</em></p>
<p><em>Review by Margaret Pomeranz</em></p>
<p>SUCKER PUNCH is most probably going to be a huge movie, particularly with young men. It's a mix of video-game, music video and adolescent wet dreams. Baby Doll, an attention-getting role for Australian actress EMILY BROWNING, is orphaned, her evil step-father attempts unspeakable things, kills her young sister and puts her away in a mental asylum with a lobotomy hovering in five days. The asylum, which has multiple realities, is run by Blue Jones, OSCAR ISAAC, as a sort of bordello - where the girls, including Sweet Pea, ABBIE CORNISH, Rocket - JENA MALONE, Blonde - VANESSA HUDGENS and Amber - JAMIE CHUNG - dance for visiting men. When Baby Doll dances she goes into another reality where, instead of being the victim, she's the one who kicks ass.<br/><br/>The five girls band together to gain five items so they can escape. It really is a video game.<br/><br/>The heightened reality, the tongue-in-cheek provocative design of Baby Doll's outfit as a mini sailor suit, has you sitting back in your seat going whoa, what's happening here? But you get into the swing of things and actually start having a good time, although the five quests become a bit repetitive. The film is surprisingly dark in tone, this is not your usual action adventure. Written by Zack Snyder and Steve Shibuya and directed by Snyder it is as you would expect from the director of 300 and WATCHMEN, a visually arresting, occasionally funny ride. Scott Glen is the guru through the quests and he quotes marvelous aphorisms like 'Don't ever write a cheque with your mouth that you can't cash with your ass.' And Jon Hamm has a small role as the lobotomizing doctor. The fact that all the performers take their somewhat ridiculous roles seriously and do them well is a major plus. But take the title seriously because that's what you the audience will get with this film.</p>
<h2>Further comments</h2>
<p>MARGARET: David.<br/><br/>DAVID: I think the opening of this film, the first maybe 10 minutes, is brilliant. It's like a short film - like a short, silent film with that Sweet Dreams Are Made Of This song going in the background and I think it shows that Zack Snyder has the potential of being a really fine director, if only he'd lift his sights a little bit because, as you say, this is really another, yawn, yawn, video game and it's just puerile. And he does it well. I'm not denying that, but surely he could do something a little bit more interesting because I've seen all this before and it's getting really boring.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, the fact that these quests are repeated five times but it's so visually exhilarating and I don't agree with you. I didn't know where the film was going and I think it goes into surprising areas and even when they're dark they're funny.<br/><br/>DAVID: I don't think it's surprising once you get into the video game mould of it. I think the opening is very surprising.<br/><br/>MARGARET: I think the scenes in the asylum are actually.<br/><br/>DAVID: Look, this could have been something really special and I think his horizons are so low. It's aimed at 12 year olds. <br/><br/>MARGARET: How come I liked it so much? <br/><br/>DAVID: Well, that's for the viewers to speculate on. What are you giving it?<br/><br/>MARGARET: I'm giving it four stars. I had a good time with this.<br/><br/>DAVID: I'm giving it three.</p>

<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[10]]<br>Appreciated this one at several levels including the surreal visual story telling The character development is great and the outstanding musical journey complements the plot so well.  The survival plot that drives the storyline is gritty and dark and sometimes just like real life you have to give everything to win but win you can.<br>The parallel reality imagining of the film demands far more of it's audience then others dare to - no straightforward action flick with the usual sugar filled centre. <h3>Stoka :</h3>
<p class="date">14 Aug 2011 1:42:03pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[10]]<br>Loved this movie for its imagination and visual complexity. I know many critics have been scathing, however I may say in Sanskrit "atmanam manyate jagat" - we all think that everyone else sees the universe as we do. however that isn't the case. I thought it was a visual revelation. Loved the stylized fight / dream sequences. I was a little disappointed in the end that the heroine was finally defeated. <li>
<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay6990_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m6990"></a>
<h3>Leigh :</h3>
<p class="date">22 Apr 2011 10:17:01pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[5]]<br/>After 300 and Watchmen, We all know the style of filmmaking to expect from Zach Snyder. The visuals in SuckerPunch, in particular the opening act are something special. He immaculately opens the story to his audience with minimal dialogue and maximum effect. Once we mindwarp with Baby Doll into the alternate reality world it is at first acceptable but rapidly becomes inconsequential, repetitious and boring! Even the scene's back at the mental facility begin to lose their worth in the final act! In the end, the visuals leave a lasting impression as pretentious and astray as the film may be.</p>

<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[7]]<br/>Let's get something straight here; this is not a video game. A video game is an interactive system of mechanics that allows the player to control the virtual world they are in. The visuals and narrative structure of Sucker Punch are similar to popular games however they are two different mediums. Games are not a watered down version of movies, as much as they appear to be at the moment. I liked the movie because it was artistically bold and didn't shy away from what it was trying to say. However it did go downhill after the phenomenal start.</p>

<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229140049/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=6783&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d243%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>Daniel Spicer :</h3>
<p class="date">13 Apr 2011 12:56:38am</p>
<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[8]]<br/>The visuals are the only real reason to see this. Visually dynamic but typically shallow, 'Sucker Punch' has an unhealthy message about escaping reality to handle your problems. There's no blood and no jokes which is disappointing, but the visuals sell the film. It's gloriously flash and fun, bold and hallucinogenic, all the while lacking grit, grain and gravity. There's a candy store of villains; , these include a dragon, androids, Nazis, giant samurai and medieval warriors. This movie is nuts.</p>

<p class="comment">((Sucker Punch))[[8]]<br/>The movie is meant to be an indictment of male nerdy culture/media. A way to holding a mirror up to it by exaggerating it so much. Baby Doll's dancing that mesmerises the men is meant to be analogous to the action scenes trying to mesmerise the movie audience. The story was simple to understand and the overall the film was a joy to watch! It's only failing seems to be what almost ended up on the cutting room floor (musical sequences that you can see in the credits).</p>

<script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">


var newtopicKey;

$(document).ready(function(){

audShow();
changeAction();
formatComments();

// end ready
});	

function audShow() {
	// display word count only if js enabled
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='inline';
	document.getElementById("audiencecomment").style.display='block';
	if (document.getElementById("allnewComments")) {
		document.getElementById("allnewComments").innerHTML = document.getElementById("loadComments").innerHTML;
	}
}


function changeAction() {
	// avoids non-js form submission 
	var tmpStoryid = "??StoryID??";
	if (document.m_frmMainForm) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229140049/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/NewMessage.aspx?b=117&amp;tn='+tmpStoryid+'&amp;dm=1&amp;tpa=&amp;r=&amp;layout=popup';
		}
}



function formatComments() {
	// replace H3 tag with 'Name:' + name
	var arrayH3 = document.getElementById("comments").getElementsByTagName("h3");
	for (var i = 0; i < arrayH3.length; i++) {
		var theString = arrayH3[i].innerHTML;
		theString = theString.replace(":", "");
		theString = "Name: "+theString;
		arrayH3[i].innerHTML = 	theString;
	}
	// add rating value to each comment
	var arrayComment = getElementsByClassName( 'comment', 'p' );	
	for (var c = 0; c < arrayComment.length; c++) {
		var theComment = arrayComment[c].innerHTML;
		theComment = theComment.replace("[[", "<span class='userRating'>Rating: <img src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141229140049/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/stars").replace("]]",".png' alt='rating'></span>").replace("((", "<!-- ").replace(")))", "))").replace("))", "-->");
		arrayComment[c].innerHTML = theComment;
	}

	
}


function formCheck(zeForm) {
	// pass key to form
	document.getElementById("keyField").value = newtopicKey;
	// basic validation
	if (document.getElementById("yname").value.length < 1) {
		alert("Please enter your name or nickname.");
		document.getElementById("yname").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (document.getElementById("yemail").value.length < 6) {
		alert("Please enter a valid email address.");
		document.getElementById("yemail").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (zeForm.score.options[0].selected && zeForm.score.options[0].value=="na") {
		alert("You forgot to rate the movie!");
		document.getElementById("score").style.background='#FFFDC8';	
		return false;
	}	
	// check for http
	spamcheck=zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	if (spamcheck.indexOf("http")!=-1) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229140049/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/blank.htm';
	}
	// check word count
	wct = cnt(zeForm.m_tbxText.value);
	if (wct > 100) {
		alert("Comments are limited to 100 words. You've written "+wct+" words!");
		document.getElementById("remark").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;	
	}
	
	// replace usual suspect bad characters 
	badChars = Array  ('', '', '', '', '', 'ö', 'é', 'è', 'ñ', 'â', ' ', '','','´');
	goodChars = Array ('...', '-', '-', '"', '"', 'o', 'e', 'e', 'n', 'a', ' ', '\'','\'','\'');
	fld = document.getElementById("remark");
	for(i=0;i<badChars.length;i++){
		restring = new RegExp( badChars[i] , 'g');
		fld.value = fld.value.replace(restring,goodChars[i]);
	}
	fldn = document.getElementById("yname");
	for(j=0;j<badChars.length;j++){
		restringj = new RegExp( badChars[j] , 'g');
		fldn.value = fldn.value.replace(restringj,goodChars[j]);
	}	
	
	// add rating to comment field in [[ ]] tags 
	var theSel = zeForm.score.selectedIndex;
	var theRating = zeForm.score[theSel].value; 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "[["+theRating+"]]\n" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	
	// add movie title to comment field in (( )) tags 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "(("+theMovie+"))" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;	
	
	// display thankyou div layer and hide form. 
	document.getElementById("favFormThx").style.display='block';
	document.getElementById("favForm").style.display='none';
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='none';	
	
	// all clear, submit the form
	return true;
}

// word count function
function cnt(theform){
	var y=theform;
	var r = 0;
	a=y.replace('\n',' ');
	a=a.split(' ');
	for (z=0; z<a.length; z++) {if (a[z].length > 0) r++;}
	return r;
}

function remainingWords(textAreaContent,textAreaContentValue, maxWords) 
{
	// Determine the number of words we have left
	var numberofwords = cnt(textAreaContentValue);
	wordsLeft = maxWords - numberofwords;
	if (wordsLeft < 1)
	{	// if 100 change color to red
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='red'; 
	} else {
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='#ffffff'; 
	}
	// update word count number
	document.getElementById("wcNum").innerHTML=(0+numberofwords);
}

// windows media alt box
function showWindows() {
	document.getElementById("windowsMed").style.display='block';
}


// generic get by class name
function getElementsByClassName(strClass, strTag, objContElm) {
  strTag = strTag || "*";
  objContElm = objContElm || document;    
  var objColl = objContElm.getElementsByTagName(strTag);
  if (!objColl.length &&  strTag == "*" &&  objContElm.all) objColl = objContElm.all;
  var arr = new Array();                              
  var delim = strClass.indexOf('|') != -1  ? '|' : ' ';   
  var arrClass = strClass.split(delim);    
  for (var i = 0, j = objColl.length; i < j; i++) {                         
    var arrObjClass = objColl[i].className.split(' ');   
    if (delim == ' ' && arrClass.length > arrObjClass.length) continue;
    var c = 0;
    comparisonLoop:
    for (var k = 0, l = arrObjClass.length; k < l; k++) {
      for (var m = 0, n = arrClass.length; m < n; m++) {
        if (arrClass[m] == arrObjClass[k]) c++;
        if ((delim == '|' && c == 1) || (delim == ' ' && c == arrClass.length)) {
          arr.push(objColl[i]); 
          break comparisonLoop;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return arr; 
}

// called from 'new discussion' page in iframe
function sayHello(theKey) {
	newtopicKey = theKey;
}

// talk to www2b iframe
document.domain = "abc.net.au";

	if((navigator.userAgent.match(/iPhone/i)) || (navigator.userAgent.match(/iPod/i)) || (navigator.userAgent.match(/iPad/i)) || (navigator.userAgent.match(/Android/i) && (androidversion > 4.05))) {
		//mobile device supports m3u8 html5 HLS video	
		$('#flashplayer').html('<img id="playerNew" src="/atthemovies/img/2011/ep09/suckerpunch_large.jpg" width="598" height="336" alt="Sucker Punch" />Video clips on this site prior to June 2012 do not play on mobile devices.');
	}
	else {
		//desktop browsers flash
		cinerama.highlightColour = "#006CD9";
		cinerama.playlistType = "horizontal"
		cinerama.embedPlayer('playerNew','rtmp://cp44823.edgefcs.net/ondemand/flash/tv/streams/atthemovies/20110406_suckerpunch_hi.flv',598,336,'',false);
	} 	
			
	
// end ready
});
